[?1049h[?1h=IWCONFIG(8)                                              Linux Programmer's Manual                                              IWCONFIG(8)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       iwconfig - configure a wireless network interface[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1miwconfig[0m [1m[[0m[4minterface[24m[1m][0m[m
       [1miwconfig[0m [4minterface[24m [1m[essid[0m [4mX[24m[1m][0m [1m[nwid[0m [4mN[24m[1m][0m [1m[mode[0m [4mM[24m[1m][0m [1m[freq[0m [4mF[24m[1m][0m[m
                          [1m[channel[0m [4mC[24m[1m][0m[4m[sens[24m [1mS[0m [4m][24m[1m[ap[0m [4mA[24m [1m][0m[4m[nick[24m [1mNN[0m [1m][0m[m
                          [1m[rate[0m [4mR[24m[1m][0m [1m[rts[0m [4mRT[24m[1m][0m [1m[frag[0m [4mFT[24m[1m][0m [1m[txpower[0m [4mT[24m[1m][0m[m
                          [1m[enc[0m [4mE[24m[1m][0m [1m[key[0m [4mK[24m[1m][0m [1m[power[0m [4mP[24m[1m][0m [1m[retry[0m [4mR[24m[1m][0m[m
                          [1m[modu[0m [4mM[24m[1m][0m [1m[commit][0m[m
       [1miwconfig[0m [1m--help[0m[m
       [1miwconfig[0m [1m--version[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mIwconfig[0m  is  similar  to  [4mifconfig[24m(8), but is dedicated to the wireless interfaces. It is used to set the parameters of the network[m
       interface which are specific to the wireless operation (for example : the frequency).  [1mIwconfig[0m may also be used  to  display  those[m
       parameters, and the wireless statistics (extracted from [4m/proc/net/wireless[24m).[m
[m
       All  these parameters and statistics are device dependent. Each driver will provide only some of them depending on hardware support,[m
       and the range of values may change. Please refer to the man page of each device for details.[m
[m
[1mPARAMETERS[0m[m
       [1messid[0m  Set the ESSID (or Network Name - in some products it may also be called Domain ID). The ESSID is used to identify cells which[m
              are part of the same virtual network.[m
              As  opposed  to the AP Address or NWID which define a single cell, the ESSID defines a group of cells connected via repeaters[m
              or infrastructure, where the user may roam transparently.[m
              With some cards, you may disable the ESSID checking (ESSID promiscuous) with [4moff[24m or [4many[24m (and [4mon[24m to reenable it).[m
              If the ESSID of your network is one of the special keywords ([4moff[24m, [4mon[24m or [4many[24m), you should use [4m--[24m to escape it.[m
              [1mExamples[0m [1m:[0m[m
                   [4miwconfig[24m [4meth0[24m [4messid[24m [4many[24m[m
                   [4miwconfig[24m [4meth0[24m [4messid[24m [4m"My[24m [4mNetwork"[24m[m
                   [4miwconfig[24m [4meth0[24m [4messid[24m [4m--[24m [4m"ANY"[24m[m
[m
       [1mnwid[0m   Set the Network ID. As all adjacent wireless networks share the same medium, this parameter is  used  to  differentiate  them[m
              (create logical colocated networks) and identify nodes belonging to the same cell.[m
              This parameter is only used for pre-802.11 hardware, the 802.11 protocol uses the ESSID and AP Address for this function.[m
              With some cards, you may disable the Network ID checking (NWID promiscuous) with [4moff[24m (and [4mon[24m to reenable it).[m
              [1mExamples[0m [1m:[0m[m
                   [4miwconfig[24m [4meth0[24m [4mnwid[24m [4mAB34[24m[m
                   [4miwconfig[24m [4meth0[24m [4mnwid[24m [4moff[24m[m
[7m Manual page iwconfig(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KAA[K[K[7m Manual page iwconfig(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       ifconfig - configure a network interface[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mifconfig[0m [1m[-v][0m [1m[-a][0m [1m[-s][0m [1m[interface][0m[m
       [1mifconfig[0m [1m[-v][0m [1minterface[0m [1m[aftype][0m [1moptions[0m [1m|[0m [1maddress[0m [1m...[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mIfconfig[0m  is  used  to configure the kernel-resident network interfaces.  It is used at boot time to set up interfaces as necessary.[m
       After that, it is usually only needed when debugging or when system tuning is needed.[m
[m
       If no arguments are given, [1mifconfig[0m displays the status of the currently active interfaces.   If  a  single  [1minterface[0m  argument  is[m
       given,  it  displays  the status of the given interface only; if a single [1m-a[0m argument is given, it displays the status of all inter‐[m
       faces, even those that are down.  Otherwise, it configures an interface.[m
[m
[1mAddress[0m [1mFamilies[0m[m
       If the first argument after the interface name is recognized as the name of a supported address family, that address family is  used[m
       for  decoding  and  displaying  all  protocol addresses.  Currently supported address families include [1minet[0m (TCP/IP, default), [1minet6[0m[m
       (IPv6), [1max25[0m (AMPR Packet Radio), [1mddp[0m (Appletalk Phase 2), [1mipx[0m (Novell IPX) and [1mnetrom[0m (AMPR Packet radio).[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-a[0m     display all interfaces which are currently available, even if down[m
[m
       [1m-s[0m     display a short list (like netstat -i)[m
[m
       [1m-v[0m     be more verbose for some error conditions[m
[m
       [1minterface[0m[m
              The name of the interface.  This is usually a driver name followed by a unit number, for example [1meth0[0m for the first  Ethernet[m
              interface.  If  your  kernel supports alias interfaces, you can specify them with [1meth0:0[0m for the first alias of eth0. You can[m
              use them to assign a second address. To delete an alias interface use [1mifconfig[0m [1meth0:0[0m [1mdown[0m.  Note: for every scope (i.e. same[m
              net with address/netmask combination) all aliases are deleted, if you delete the first (primary).[m
[m
       [1mup[0m     This flag causes the interface to be activated.  It is implicitly specified if an address is assigned to the interface.[m
[m
       [1mdown[0m   This flag causes the driver for this interface to be shut down.[m
[m
       [1m[-]arp[0m Enable or disable the use of the ARP protocol on this interface.[m
[m
       [1m[-]promisc[0m[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Enable  or  disable  the  [1mpromiscuous[0m mode of the interface.  If selected, all packets on the network will be received by the[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              interface.[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1m[-]allmulti[0m[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Enable or disable [1mall-multicast[0m mode.  If selected, all multicast packets on the network will be received by the interface.[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1mmetric[0m [1mN[0m[m

[43;1H[K[7m Manual page ifconfig(8) line 1/138 32% (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K              Enable  or  disable  the  [1mpromiscuous[0m mode of the interface.  If selected, all packets on the network will be received by the[m
              interface.[m
[m
       [1m[-]allmulti[0m[m
              Enable or disable [1mall-multicast[0m mode.  If selected, all multicast packets on the network will be received by the interface.[m
[m
       [1mmetric[0m [1mN[0m[m
              This parameter sets the interface metric.[m
[m
       [1mmtu[0m [1mN[0m  This parameter sets the Maximum Transfer Unit (MTU) of an interface.[m
[m
       [1mdstaddr[0m [1maddr[0m[m
              Set the remote IP address for a point-to-point link (such as PPP).  This keyword is now obsolete; use the [1mpointopoint[0m keyword[m
              instead.[m
[m
       [1mnetmask[0m [1maddr[0m[m
              Set  the  IP network mask for this interface.  This value defaults to the usual class A, B or C network mask (as derived from[m
              the interface IP address), but it can be set to any value.[m
[m
       [1madd[0m [1maddr/prefixlen[0m[m
              Add an IPv6 address to an interface.[m
[m
       [1mdel[0m [1maddr/prefixlen[0m[m
              Remove an IPv6 address from an interface.[m
[m
       [1mtunnel[0m [1maa.bb.cc.dd[0m[m
              Create a new SIT (IPv6-in-IPv4) device, tunnelling to the given destination.[m
[m
       [1mirq[0m [1maddr[0m[m
              Set the interrupt line used by this device.  Not all devices can dynamically change their IRQ setting.[m
[m
       [1mio_addr[0m [1maddr[0m[m
              Set the start address in I/O space for this device.[m
[m
       [1mmem_start[0m [1maddr[0m[m
              Set the start address for shared memory used by this device.  Only a few devices need this.[m
[m
       [1mmedia[0m [1mtype[0m[m
              Set the physical port or medium type to be used by the device.  Not all devices can change this setting, and those  that  can[m
              vary  in  what values they support.  Typical values for [1mtype[0m are [1m10base2[0m (thin Ethernet), [1m10baseT[0m (twisted-pair 10Mbps Ether‐[m
              net), [1mAUI[0m (external transceiver) and so on.  The special medium type of [1mauto[0m can be used to tell the driver to auto-sense the[m
              media.  Again, not all drivers can do this.[m

                   [1mSUMMARY[0m [1mOF[0m [1mLESS[0m [1mCOMMANDS[0m[m
[m
      Commands marked with * may be preceded by a number, [4mN[24m.[m
      Notes in parentheses indicate the behavior if [4mN[24m is given.[m
      A key preceded by a caret indicates the Ctrl key; thus ^K is ctrl-K.[m
[m
  h  H                 Display this help.[m
  q  :q  Q  :Q  ZZ     Exit.[m
 ---------------------------------------------------------------------------[m
[m
                           [1mMOVING[0m[m
[m
  e  ^E  j  ^N  CR  *  Forward  one line   (or [4mN[24m lines).[m
  y  ^Y  k  ^K  ^P  *  Backward one line   (or [4mN[24m lines).[m
  f  ^F  ^V  SPACE  *  Forward  one window (or [4mN[24m lines).[m
  b  ^B  ESC-v      *  Backward one window (or [4mN[24m lines).[m
  z                 *  Forward  one window (and set window to [4mN[24m).[m
  w                 *  Backward one window (and set window to [4mN[24m).[m
  ESC-SPACE         *  Forward  one window, but don't stop at end-of-file.[m
  d  ^D             *  Forward  one half-window (and set half-window to [4mN[24m).[m
  u  ^U             *  Backward one half-window (and set half-window to [4mN[24m).[m
  ESC-)  RightArrow *  Left  one half screen width (or [4mN[24m positions).[m
  ESC-(  LeftArrow  *  Right one half screen width (or [4mN[24m positions).[m
  F                    Forward forever; like "tail -f".[m
  ESC-F                Like F but stop when search pattern is found.[m
  r  ^R  ^L            Repaint screen.[m
  R                    Repaint screen, discarding buffered input.[m
        ---------------------------------------------------[m
        Default "window" is the screen height.[m
        Default "half-window" is half of the screen height.[m
 ---------------------------------------------------------------------------[m
[m
                          [1mSEARCHING[0m[m
[m
  /[4mpattern[24m          *  Search forward for ([4mN[24m-th) matching line.[m
  ?[4mpattern[24m          *  Search backward for ([4mN[24m-th) matching line.[m
  n                 *  Repeat previous search (for [4mN[24m-th occurrence).[m
  N                 *  Repeat previous search in reverse direction.[m
  ESC-n             *  Repeat previous search, spanning files.[m
  ESC-N             *  Repeat previous search, reverse dir. & spanning files.[m
  ESC-u                Undo (toggle) search highlighting.[m
[7mHELP -- Press RETURN for more, or q when done[27m[K[K:[K00[K  &[4mpattern[24m          *  Display only matching lines[m
        ---------------------------------------------------[m
        A search pattern may be preceded by one or more of:[m
        ^N or !  Search for NON-matching lines.[m
        ^E or *  Search multiple files (pass thru END OF FILE).[m
        ^F or @  Start search at FIRST file (for /) or last file (for ?).[m
        ^K       Highlight matches, but don't move (KEEP position).[m
        ^R       Don't use REGULAR EXPRESSIONS.[m
 ---------------------------------------------------------------------------[m
[m
                           [1mJUMPING[0m[m
[m
  g  <  ESC-<       *  Go to first line in file (or line [4mN[24m).[m
  G  >  ESC->       *  Go to last line in file (or line [4mN[24m).[m
  p  %              *  Go to beginning of file (or [4mN[24m percent into file).[m
  t                 *  Go to the ([4mN[24m-th) next tag.[m
  T                 *  Go to the ([4mN[24m-th) previous tag.[m
  {  (  [           *  Find close bracket } ) ].[m
  }  )  ]           *  Find open bracket { ( [.[m
  ESC-^F [4m<c1>[24m [4m<c2>[24m  *  Find close bracket [4m<c2>[24m.[m
  ESC-^B [4m<c1>[24m [4m<c2>[24m  *  Find open bracket [4m<c1>[24m [m
        ---------------------------------------------------[m
        Each "find close bracket" command goes forward to the close bracket [m
          matching the ([4mN[24m-th) open bracket in the top line.[m
        Each "find open bracket" command goes backward to the open bracket [m
          matching the ([4mN[24m-th) close bracket in the bottom line.[m
[m
  m[4m<letter>[24m            Mark the current position with <letter>.[m
  '[4m<letter>[24m            Go to a previously marked position.[m
  ''                   Go to the previous position.[m
  ^X^X                 Same as '.[m
        ---------------------------------------------------[m
        A mark is any upper-case or lower-case letter.[m
        Certain marks are predefined:[m
             ^  means  beginning of the file[m
             $  means  end of the file[m
 ---------------------------------------------------------------------------[m

                  Forward scroll limit.[m
  -z [[4mN[24m]  ....  --window=[[4mN[24m][m
                  Set size of window.[m
  -" [[4mc[24m[[4mc[24m]]  .  --quotes=[[4mc[24m[[4mc[24m]][m
                  Set shell quote characters.[m
  -~  ........  --tilde[m
                  Don't display tildes after end of file.[m
  -# [[4mN[24m]  ....  --shift=[[4mN[24m][m
                  Horizontal scroll amount (0 = one half screen width)[m
      ........  --no-keypad[m
                  Don't send termcap keypad init/deinit strings.[m
      ........  --follow-name[m
                  The F command changes files if the input file is renamed.[m
      ........  --use-backslash[m
                  Subsequent options use backslash as escape char.[m

                          [1mLINE[0m [1mEDITING[0m[m
[m
        These keys can be used to edit text being entered [m
        on the "command line" at the bottom of the screen.[m
[m
 RightArrow ..................... ESC-l ... Move cursor right one character.[m
 LeftArrow ...................... ESC-h ... Move cursor left one character.[m
 ctrl-RightArrow  ESC-RightArrow  ESC-w ... Move cursor right one word.[m
 ctrl-LeftArrow   ESC-LeftArrow   ESC-b ... Move cursor left one word.[m
 HOME ........................... ESC-0 ... Move cursor to start of line.[m
 END ............................ ESC-$ ... Move cursor to end of line.[m
 BACKSPACE ................................ Delete char to left of cursor.[m
 DELETE ......................... ESC-x ... Delete char under cursor.[m
 ctrl-BACKSPACE   ESC-BACKSPACE ........... Delete word to left of cursor.[m
 ctrl-DELETE .... ESC-DELETE .... ESC-X ... Delete word under cursor.[m
 ctrl-U ......... ESC (MS-DOS only) ....... Delete entire line.[m
 UpArrow ........................ ESC-k ... Retrieve previous command line.[m
 DownArrow ...................... ESC-j ... Retrieve next command line.[m
 TAB ...................................... Complete filename & cycle.[m
 SHIFT-TAB ...................... ESC-TAB   Complete filename & reverse cycle.[m
 ctrl-L ................................... Complete filename, list all.[m

                           [1mOPTIONS[0m[m
[m
        Most options may be changed either on the command line,[m
        or from within less by using the - or -- command.[m
        Options may be given in one of two forms: either a single[m
        character preceded by a -, or a name preceded by --.[m
[m
  -?  ........  --help[m
                  Display help (from command line).[m
  -a  ........  --search-skip-screen[m
                  Search skips current screen.[m
  -A  ........  --SEARCH-SKIP-SCREEN[m
                  Search starts just after target line.[m
  -b [[4mN[24m]  ....  --buffers=[[4mN[24m][m
                  Number of buffers.[m
  -B  ........  --auto-buffers[m
                  Don't automatically allocate buffers for pipes.[m
  -c  ........  --clear-screen[m
                  Repaint by clearing rather than scrolling.[m
  -d  ........  --dumb[m
                  Dumb terminal.[m
[7mHELP -- Press RETURN for more, or q when done[27m[K[K[7mHELP -- Press RETURN for more, or q when done[27m[K[K[H[2J[HM  ESC-u                Undo (toggle) search highlighting.[m

[HM  ?[4mpattern[24m          *  Search backward for ([4mN[24m-th) matching line.[m
[HM  /[4mpattern[24m          *  Search forward for ([4mN[24m-th) matching line.[m

[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       route - show / manipulate the IP routing table[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mroute[0m [[1m-CFvnee[0m][m
[m
       [1mroute[0m  [[1m-v[0m]  [[1m-A[0m  family]  [1madd[0m  [[1m-net[0m|[1m-host[0m] target [[1mnetmask[0m Nm] [[1mgw[0m Gw] [[1mmetric[0m N] [[1mmss[0m M] [[1mwindow[0m W] [[1mirtt[0m I] [[1mreject[0m] [[1mmod[0m] [[1mdyn[0m][m
              [[1mreinstate[0m] [[[1mdev[0m] If][m
[m
       [1mroute[0m  [[1m-v[0m] [[1m-A[0m family] [1mdel[0m [[1m-net[0m|[1m-host[0m] target [[1mgw[0m Gw] [[1mnetmask[0m Nm] [[1mmetric[0m N] [[[1mdev[0m] If][m
[m
       [1mroute[0m  [[1m-V[0m] [[1m--version[0m] [[1m-h[0m] [[1m--help[0m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mRoute[0m manipulates the kernel's IP routing tables.  Its primary use is to set up static routes to specific hosts or networks  via  an[m
       interface after it has been configured with the [1mifconfig[0m(8) program.[m
[m
       When the [1madd[0m or [1mdel[0m options are used, [1mroute[0m modifies the routing tables.  Without these options, [1mroute[0m displays the current contents[m
       of the routing tables.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-A[0m [1mfamily[0m[m
              use the specified address family (eg `inet'; use `route --help' for a full list).[m
[m
       [1m-F[0m     operate on the kernel's FIB (Forwarding Information Base) routing table.  This is the default.[m
[m
       [1m-C[0m     operate on the kernel's routing cache.[m
[m
       [1m-v[0m     select verbose operation.[m
[m
       [1m-n[0m     show numerical addresses instead of trying to determine symbolic host names. This is useful if you are  trying  to  determine[m
              why the route to your nameserver has vanished.[m
[m
       [1m-e[0m     use  [1mnetstat[0m(8)-format  for  displaying  the  routing table.  [1m-ee[0m will generate a very long line with all parameters from the[m
              routing table.[m
[m
       [1mdel[0m    delete a route.[m
[m
       [1madd[0m    add a new route.[m
[m

[7m Manual page route(8) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       [1mreject[0m install a blocking route, which will force a route lookup to fail.  This is for example used  to  mask  out  networks  before[m
